# Task: Implement Custom Header Injection Filter for Envoy

## Objective
Create a new HTTP filter `envoy.filters.http.custom_header_injection` that injects
configurable headers into requests and/or responses based on route metadata.

## Requirements

1. **Create filter source files**:
   - `source/extensions/filters/http/custom_header_injection/filter.h` — filter class declaration
   - `source/extensions/filters/http/custom_header_injection/filter.cc` — filter implementation
   - `source/extensions/filters/http/custom_header_injection/config.h` — factory declaration
   - `source/extensions/filters/http/custom_header_injection/config.cc` — factory registration

2. **Filter behavior**:
   - Implements `Http::StreamDecoderFilter` (request path) and `Http::StreamEncoderFilter` (response path)
   - Reads header injection rules from filter config
   - Supports both request and response header injection
   - Follows Envoy's filter lifecycle (decodeHeaders, encodeHeaders)

3. **Create test file**:
   - `test/extensions/filters/http/custom_header_injection/filter_test.cc`

## Key Reference Files
- `source/extensions/filters/http/header_to_metadata/filter.h` — simple header filter pattern
- `source/extensions/filters/http/header_to_metadata/filter.cc` — implementation pattern
- `source/extensions/filters/http/header_to_metadata/config.cc` — factory registration
- `source/extensions/filters/http/common/factory_base.h` — factory base class

## Success Criteria
- Filter header file declares class inheriting from StreamDecoderFilter/StreamEncoderFilter
- Filter implementation has decodeHeaders/encodeHeaders methods
- Factory config file registers the filter
- Follows Envoy naming: envoy.filters.http.custom_header_injection
- Test file exists

1172026-03-11T05:13:42.555023agentmessage-
I am thinking...: Now I have a clear picture of how to implement the filter. Let me design the filter:

1. `FilterConfig` - holds global `HeaderParser` instances for request and response headers
2. `PerRouteFilterConfig` - holds per-route `HeaderParser` instances, extends `Router::RouteSpecificFilterConfig`
3. `CustomHeaderInjectionFilter` - the actual filter, extends `PassThroughFilter`
   - In `decodeHeaders`: apply global request headers, then per-route request headers
   - In `encodeHeaders`: apply global response headers, then per-route response headers

Key design decisions:
- Use `Router::HeaderParser` for header injection (supports format strings, append actions)
- Use `Http::Utility::resolveMostSpecificPerFilterConfig` to get per-route config
- Use `THROW_OR_RETURN_VALUE` for HeaderParser::configure in constructors (since constructors can't return StatusOr)
- Use `absl::StatusOr` for factory methods

For the filter constructor, I need to handle the case where `HeaderParser::configure` might fail. Looking at the local_ratelimit pattern, they use `THROW_OR_RETURN_VALUE` in the constructor initializer list. But the header_mutation filter uses `absl::Status& creation_status` pattern. Let me use the creation_status pattern since it's more modern.

Actually, looking at the header_mutation filter more carefully:

```cpp
HeaderMutationConfig(const ProtoConfig& config, absl::Status& creation_status);
```

And in the factory:
```cpp
auto filter_config = std::make_shared<HeaderMutationConfig>(config, creation_status);
RETURN_IF_NOT_OK_REF(creation_status);
```

I'll use the same pattern for FilterConfig and PerRouteFilterConfig.

For the filter itself, it just takes a `std::shared_ptr<FilterConfig>` and doesn't need error handling in the constructor.

I am thinking...: Let me carefully review the `RouteConfigsInitializedOnlyOnce` test. 

In this test:
1. `decodeHeaders` is called → `initializeRouteConfigs(decoder_callbacks_)` is called → `getAllPerFilterConfig<PerRouteFilterConfig>(decoder_callbacks_)` → `decoder_callbacks_->perFilterConfigs()` → `decoder_callbacks.route_->perFilterConfigs("envoy.filter")` → returns `{route_config.get()}`
2. `encodeHeaders` is called → `initializeRouteConfigs(encoder_callbacks_)` is called → BUT `route_configs_initialized_` is already `true`, so it returns immediately without calling `encoder_callbacks_->perFilterConfigs()`

The test sets `EXPECT_CALL(*decoder_callbacks.route_, perFilterConfigs(_)).WillOnce(...)` — this means it expects exactly ONE call to `decoder_callbacks.route_->perFilterConfigs(_)`. Since `encoder_callbacks_` is a different mock object, and `encoder_callbacks.route_` is a different mock, there's no expectation set on `encoder_callbacks.route_->perFilterConfigs(_)`.

Wait, but `NiceMock` will allow unexpected calls without failing. So even if `encoder_callbacks.route_->perFilterConfigs(_)` is called, it won't fail the test. The `WillOnce` on `decoder_callbacks.route_` ensures it's called exactly once on the decoder side.

Actually, `WillOnce` with `EXPECT_CALL` means it expects exactly one call. If it's called more than once, the test fails. If it's called zero times, the test also fails (because `EXPECT_CALL` with `WillOnce` implies `Times(1)` by default).

So the test correctly verifies that `decoder_callbacks.route_->perFilterConfigs(_)` is called exactly once (during `decodeHeaders`), and `encoder_callbacks.route_->perFilterConfigs(_)` is never called (because `route_configs_initialized_` is already true when `encodeHeaders` runs).

This is correct behavior.

2472026-03-11T05:26:54.940305agentmessage-
I am thinking...: I see! The pattern for `DualFactoryBase` is to create a type alias for the upstream factory:

```cpp
using UpstreamAdmissionControlFilterFactory = AdmissionControlFilterFactory;
```

And then register both:
```cpp
REGISTER_FACTORY(AdmissionControlFilterFactory, Server::Configuration::NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory);
REGISTER_FACTORY(UpstreamAdmissionControlFilterFactory, Server::Configuration::UpstreamHttpFilterConfigFactory);
```

This is because `REGISTER_FACTORY` uses the type name as part of the registration, and you can't register the same type twice for different interfaces. The type alias creates a distinct registration.

Our current `config.cc` does:
```cpp
REGISTER_FACTORY(CustomHeaderInjectionFactoryConfig, Server::Configuration::NamedHttpFilterConfigFactory);
REGISTER_FACTORY(CustomHeaderInjectionFactoryConfig, Server::Configuration::UpstreamHttpFilterConfigFactory);
```

This is wrong! We need to create a type alias and use that for the upstream registration. Let me fix this.

Let me check another example to confirm.

The issue with `REGISTER_FACTORY` is that the macro creates:

- `REGISTER_FACTORY(UpstreamCustomHeaderInjectionFactoryConfig, UpstreamHttpFilterConfigFactory)` creates `forceRegisterUpstreamCustomHeaderInjectionFactoryConfig()` and `UpstreamCustomHeaderInjectionFactoryConfig_registered`

134\t  route_configs_ = Http::Utility::getAllPerFilterConfig<PerRouteHeaderMutation>(callbacks);\n   135\t\n   136\t  // The order of returned route configs is route table first, then virtual host, HeaderMutation::maybeInitializeRouteConfigs(Http::StreamFilterCallbacks* callbacks) {\n  // Ensure that route configs are initialized only once and the same route configs are used\n  // for both decoding and encoding paths.\n  // An independent flag is used to ensure even at the case where the route configs is empty,\n  // we still won't try to initialize it again.\n  if Http::Utility::getAllPerFilterConfig<PerRouteHeaderMutation>(callbacks);\n\n  // The order of returned route configs is route table first, then virtual host, then\n  // per route. That means the per route configs will be evaluated at the end and will\n  // override the more general virtual host and route table configs.\n  //\n  // So, if most_specific_header_mutations_wins is false, we need to reverse the order\n  // of route configs.\n  if (!config_->mostSpecificHeaderMutationsWins()) {\n    std::reverse(route_configs_.begin(), route_configs_.end());\n  }\n}\n\nHttp::FilterHeadersStatus HeaderMutation::decodeHeaders(Http::RequestHeaderMap& headers, bool) {\n  Formatter::HttpFormatterContext context{&headers};\n  config_->mutations().mutateRequestHeaders(headers, context, decoder_callbacks_->streamInfo());\n\n  maybeInitializeRouteConfigs(decoder_callbacks_);\n\n  for (const PerRouteHeaderMutation& route_config : route_configs_) {\n    route_config.mutations().mutateRequestHeaders(headers, context,\n                                                  decoder_callbacks_->streamInfo());\n  }\n\n  return Http::FilterHeadersStatus::Continue;\n}\n\nHttp::FilterHeadersStatus HeaderMutation::encodeHeaders(Http::ResponseHeaderMap& headers, bool) {\n  Formatter::HttpFormatterContext context{encoder_callbacks_->requestHeaders().ptr(), &headers};\n  config_->mutations().mutateResponseHeaders(headers, context, encoder_callbacks_->streamInfo());\n\n  // Note if the filter before this one has send local reply then the decodeHeaders() will not be\n  // be called and the route config will not be initialized. The `header_mutation` filter uses a custom `HeaderMutations` class (from `source/common/http/header_mutation.h`) which is different from `Router::HeaderParser`. \n\nFor our `custom_header_injection` filter, we're using `config.core.v3.HeaderValueOption` directly (like `local_ratelimit` does), so we should use `Router::HeaderParser::configure()` which accepts `Protobuf::RepeatedPtrField<HeaderValueOption>`.\n\nThe key difference from `header_mutation`:\n- `header_mutation` uses `config.common.mutation_rules.v3.HeaderMutation` (which supports remove + append)\n- Our filter uses `config.core.v3.HeaderValueOption` (which only supports add/overwrite, no remove)\n\nThis is simpler and more like `local_ratelimit`.\n\nFor the filter implementation:\n1. `FilterConfig` - holds `Router::HeaderParserPtr` for request and response headers, constructed with `absl::Status& creation_status`\n2. `PerRouteFilterConfig : public Router::RouteSpecificFilterConfig` - same pattern\n3. `CustomHeaderInjectionFilter : public Http::PassThroughFilter, public Logger::Loggable<Logger::Id::filter>`\n\nFor the `FilterConfig` constructor, I'll use `THROW_OR_RETURN_VALUE` pattern (like local_ratelimit) since it's simpler for initializer lists, OR I'll use the `absl::Status& creation_status` pattern (like header_mutation) which is more modern.\n\nActually, looking at the factory code for header_mutation:\n```cpp\nauto filter_config = std::make_shared<HeaderMutationConfig>(config, creation_status);\nRETURN_IF_NOT_OK_REF(creation_status);\n```\n\nThis is the preferred pattern. Let me use this for our filter too.\n\nFor `FilterConfig`:\n```cpp\nFilterConfig(const ProtoConfig& config, absl::Status& creation_status) {\n  auto req_parser = Router::HeaderParser::configure(config.request_headers_to_add());\n  SET_AND_RETURN_IF_NOT_OK(req_parser.status(), creation_status);\n  request_headers_parser_ = std::move(req_parser.value());\n  \n  auto resp_parser = Router::HeaderParser::configure(config.response_headers_to_add());\n  SET_AND_RETURN_IF_NOT_OK(resp_parser.status(), creation_status);\n  response_headers_parser_ = std::move(resp_parser.value());\n}\n```\n\nFor the filter's `decodeHeaders` and `encodeHeaders`, I'll use `evaluateHeaders` with `streamInfo()`.\n\nFor per-route configs, I'll use `Http::Utility::getAllPerFilterConfig<PerRouteFilterConfig>` to get all configs in order (from least specific to most specific), and apply them in that order (so most specific wins).\n\nLet me now write the filter.h and filter.cc files.\n"
